It is expected\n    55→// that objects may implement any of the below interfaces.\n    56→//\n    57→// Consider using StorageWithReadiness whenever possible.\n    58→type Storage interface {\n    59→\t// New returns an empty object that can be used with Create and Update after request data has been put into it.\n    60→\t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n    61→\tNew() runtime.Object\n    62→\n    63→\t// Destroy cleans up its resources on shutdown.\n    64→\t// Destroy has to be implemented in thread-safe way and be prepared\n    65→\t// for being called more than once.\n    66→\tDestroy()\n    67→}\n    68→\n    69→// StorageWithReadiness extends Storage interface with the readiness check.\n    70→type StorageWithReadiness interface {\n    71→\tStorage\n    72→\n    73→\t// ReadinessCheck allows for checking storage readiness.\n    74→\tReadinessCheck() error\n    75→}\n    76→\n    77→// Scoper indicates what scope the resource is at. It must be specified.\n    78→// It is usually provided automatically based on your strategy.\n    79→type Scoper interface {\n    80→\t// NamespaceScoped returns true if the storage is namespaced\n    81→\tNamespaceScoped() bool\n    82→}\n    83→\n    84→// KindProvider specifies a different kind for its API than for its internal storage.  This is necessary for external\n    85→// objects that are not compiled into the api server.  For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\n    86→// the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\n    87→// API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\n    88→type KindProvider interface {\n    89→\tKind() string\n    90→}\n    91→\n    92→// ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. Delivers a list of short names for a resource. The list is used by kubectl to have short names representation of resources.\n    93→type ShortNamesProvider interface {\n    94→\tShortNames() []string\n    95→}\n    96→\n    97→// CategoriesProvider allows a resource to specify which groups of resources (categories) it's part of. Categories can\n    98→// be used by API clients to refer to a batch of resources by using a single name (e.g. \"all\" could translate to \"pod,rc,svc,...\").\n    99→type CategoriesProvider interface {\n   100→\tCategories() []string\n   101→}\n   102→\n   103→// SingularNameProvider returns singular name of resources. This is used by kubectl discovery to have singular\n   104→// name representation of resources. In case of shortcut conflicts(with CRD shortcuts) singular name should always map to this resource.\n   105→type SingularNameProvider interface {\n   106→\tGetSingularName() string\n   107→}\n   108→\n   109→// GroupVersionKindProvider is used to specify a particular GroupVersionKind to discovery.  This is used for polymorphic endpoints\n   110→// which generally point to foreign versions. Definitions**\n**File:** `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/rest/rest.go`\n\nKey interfaces that define what verbs a storage implementation supports:\n\n- **`Creater`** (line 201): `Create(ctx, obj, validation, options)` - implements POST\n- **`Getter`** (line 136): `Get(ctx, name, options)` - implements GET for single resource\n- **`Lister`** (line 125): `List(ctx, options)` - implements LIST\n- **`Updater`** (line 264): `Update(ctx, name, objInfo, ...)` - implements PUT\n- **`Patcher`** (line 286): Combines Getter and Updater - implements PATCH\n- **`GracefulDeleter`** (line 170): `Delete(ctx, name, validation, options)` - implements DELETE\n- **`CollectionDeleter`** (line 191): `DeleteCollection(...)` - implements DELETE on collections\n- **`Watcher`** (line 293): `Watch(ctx, options)` - implements WATCH\n- **`Connecter`** (line 334): `Connect(ctx, id, options, responder)` - implements CONNECT\n\n### 4. **Verb Enforcement During Route Installation**\n**File:** `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` (lines 333-594)\n\nThe installer checks which interfaces the storage implements using type assertions:\n\n```go\n// Type assertions check which verbs are supported\ncreater, isCreater := storage.(rest.Creater)\nlister, isLister := storage.(rest.Lister)\ngetter, isGetter := storage.(rest.Getter)\ngracefulDeleter, isGracefulDeleter := storage.(rest.GracefulDeleter)\nupdater, isUpdater := storage.(rest.Updater)\npatcher, isPatcher := storage.(rest.Patcher)\nwatcher, isWatcher := storage.(rest.Watcher)\n```\n\nThen actions are conditionally appended based on these checks:\n\n```go\n// Only add action if storage implements the interface\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"LIST\", ...}, isLister)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"POST\", ...}, isCreater)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"GET\", ...}, isGetter)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"PUT\", ...}, isUpdater)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"PATCH\", ...}, isPatcher)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"DELETE\", ...}, isGracefulDeleter)\nactions = appendIf(actions, action{\"WATCH\", ...}, isWatcher)\n```\n\n### 5. **Generic Registry Implementation**\n**File:** `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`\n\nThe `Store` type provides the standard REST CRUD implementations:\n\n- `Create()` (line 446) - implements `rest.Creater`\n- `List()` (line 368) - implements `rest.Lister`\n- `Get()` (line 844) - implements `rest.Getter`\n- `Update()` (line 617) - implements `rest.Updater`\n- Implicitly supports `rest.Patcher` (combines Getter+Updater)\n- Supports deletion through `rest.GracefulDeleter`\n- Supports `rest.Watcher`\n\n### 6. **Storage Implementation Example**\n**File:** `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/pkg/registry/admissionregistration/mutatingadmissionpolicy/storage/storage.go`\n\nConcrete storage implementations embed `genericregistry.Store` and inherit all CRUD operations:\n\n```go\ntype REST struct {\n    *genericregistry.Store\n}\n\n// Automatically implements: Creater, Getter, Lister, Updater, GracefulDeleter, \n// CollectionDeleter, Watcher, and Patcher interfaces\n```\n\n### Key Enforcement Points:\n\n1. **Type assertion checking** - The installer uses Go type assertions to detect which interfaces a storage implements\n2. **Conditional action registration** - Only HTTP routes are registered if the corresponding interface is implemented\n3. **Discovery verb mapping** - The `toDiscoveryKubeVerb` map ensures consistency between internal verbs and API discovery\n4. **No mismatch possible** - If a storage doesn't implement an interface, the verb/HTTP method won't be available at all\n\nThis is a robust design that prevents HTTP method to verb mismatches by only registering routes for verbs that the underlying storage actually
